# End-to-End: How Kubernetes Creates a Deployment

## Your Task

You are onboarding to the Kubernetes project. A senior engineer has asked you to produce
a technical explanation of how a Kubernetes Deployment gets created — tracing the full
request flow from a client application through the API server and into persistent storage.

**Your question**: Explain how a Kubernetes client application creates a Deployment from
start to finish. Your explanation must trace through all three layers:

1. **Client library** — What type/function in `kubernetes-client-go` sends the HTTP request?
2. **API server** — What function in `kubernetes/kubernetes` receives and validates the create request?
3. **Storage** — What function in `etcd-io/etcd` persists the Deployment to the key-value store?

For each step, cite the specific repository, file path, and function/type name.

## Context

You are working in a Kubernetes ecosystem with the following repos:

- Local `/workspace/kubernetes/` — `kubernetes/kubernetes` (the core orchestrator)
- Accessible via Sourcegraph MCP:
  - `sg-benchmarks/kubernetes-client-go` (go-client-library)
  - `sg-benchmarks/kubernetes-api` (api-type-definitions)
  - `etcd-io/etcd` (distributed-kv-store)

This question is specifically designed to benefit from cross-repo synthesis. Use your
search tools to trace the full path across repositories.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings:

```json
{
  "chain": [
    {
      "repo": "sg-benchmarks/kubernetes-client-go",
      "path": "relative/path/to/file.go",
      "symbol": "FunctionOrTypeName",
      "description": "What this step does in the flow"
    }
  ],
  "text": "Comprehensive narrative explaining the end-to-end flow, citing specific files and functions from each repo."
}
```

**Important**: Use exact repo identifiers as they appear in Sourcegraph. The oracle expects `repo` values of `sg-benchmarks/kubernetes-client-go` (client layer), `kubernetes/kubernetes` (API server layer), and `etcd-io/etcd` (storage layer). The `repo` field must match these exactly.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes-client-go`). Strip this prefix in your answer — use `sg-benchmarks/kubernetes-client-go`, NOT `github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes-client-go`.

The `chain` should contain at least 3 steps representing the 3 layers described above.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **Flow coverage**: Does the chain include key steps from all 3 layers (client → server → storage)?
- **Technical accuracy**: Are the cited file paths and function names correct?
- **Provenance**: Does your narrative reference all three repositories?
- **Synthesis quality** (supplementary): Does the explanation connect the layers clearly?

   101→
   102→func (tw *storeTxnWrite) DeleteRange(key, end []byte) (int64, int64) {
   103→	if n := tw.deleteRange(key, end); n != 0 || len(tw.changes) > 0 {
   104→		return n, tw.beginRev + 1
   105→	}
   106→	return 0, tw.beginRev
   107→}
   108→
   109→func (tw *storeTxnWrite) Put(key, value []byte, lease lease.LeaseID) int64 {
   110→	tw.put(key, value, lease)
   111→	return tw.beginRev + 1
   112→}
   113→
   114→func (tw *storeTxnWrite) End() {
   115→	// only update index if the txn modifies the mvcc state.
   116→	if len(tw.changes) != 0 {
   117→		// hold revMu lock to prevent new read txns from opening until writeback.
   118→		tw.s.revMu.Lock()
   119→		tw.s.currentRev++
   120→	}
   121→	tw.tx.Unlock()
   122→	if len(tw.changes) != 0 {
   123→		tw.s.revMu.Unlock()
   124→	}
   125→	tw.s.mu.RUnlock()
   126→}
   127→
   128→func (tr *storeTxnRead) rangeKeys(ctx context.Context, key, end []byte, curRev int64, ro RangeOptions) (*RangeResult, error) {
   129→	rev := ro.Rev
   130→	if rev > curRev {
   131→		return &RangeResult{KVs: nil, Count: -1, Rev: curRev}, ErrFutureRev
   132→	}
   133→	if rev <= 0 {
   134→		rev = curRev
   135→	}
   136→	if rev < tr.s.compactMainRev {
   137→		return &RangeResult{KVs: nil, Count: -1, Rev: 0}, ErrCompacted
   138→	}
   139→	if ro.Count {
   140→		total := tr.s.kvindex.CountRevisions(key, end, rev)
   141→		tr.trace.Step("count revisions from in-memory index tree")
   142→		return &RangeResult{KVs: nil, Count: total, Rev: curRev}, nil
   143→	}
   144→	revpairs, total := tr.s.kvindex.Revisions(key, end, rev, int(ro.Limit))
   145→	tr.trace.Step("range keys from in-memory index tree")
   146→	if len(revpairs) == 0 {
   147→		return &RangeResult{KVs: nil, Count: total, Rev: curRev}, nil
   148→	}
   149→

    30→type Bucket interface {
    31→	// ID returns a unique identifier of a bucket.
    32→	// The id must NOT be persisted and can be used as lightweight identificator
    33→	// in the in-memory maps.

    35→	Name() []byte
    36→	// String implements Stringer (human readable name).

    38→

    40→	// overwrites on a bucket should only fetch with limit=1, but safeRangeBucket
    41→	// is known to never overwrite any key so range is safe.
    42→	IsSafeRangeBucket() bool
    43→}

   243→// Create takes the representation of a resource and creates it.  Returns the server's representation of the resource, and an error, if there is any.
   244→func (c *Client[T]) Create(ctx context.Context, obj T, opts metav1.CreateOptions) (T, error) {
   245→	result := c.newObject()
   246→	err := c.client.Post().
   247→		UseProtobufAsDefaultIfPreferred(c.prefersProtobuf).
   248→		NamespaceIfScoped(c.namespace, c.namespace != "").
   249→		Resource(c.resource).
   250→		VersionedParams(&opts, c.parameterCodec).
   251→		Body(obj).
   252→		Do(ctx).
   253→		Into(result)
   254→	return result, err
   255→}
   256→
   257→// Update takes the representation of a resource and updates it. Returns the server's representation of the resource, and an error, if there is any.
   258→func (c *Client[T]) Update(ctx context.Context, obj T, opts metav1.UpdateOptions) (T, error) {
   259→	result := c.newObject()
   260→	err := c.client.Put().
   261→		UseProtobufAsDefaultIfPreferred(c.prefersProtobuf).
   262→		NamespaceIfScoped(c.namespace, c.namespace != "").
   263→		Resource(c.resource).
   264→		Name(obj.GetName()).
   265→		VersionedParams(&opts, c.parameterCodec).
   266→		Body(obj).
   267→		Do(ctx).
   268→		Into(result)
   269→	return result, err
   270→}

   454→// needsNameGeneration returns true if the obj has a generateName but no name.
   455→func needsNameGeneration(obj runtime.Object) bool {

   459→		}
   460→	}
   461→	return false
   462→}

   454→// needsNameGeneration returns true if the obj has a generateName but no name.
   455→func needsNameGeneration(obj runtime.Object) bool {
   456→	if objectMeta, err := meta.Accessor(obj); err == nil {
   457→		if len(objectMeta.GetGenerateName()) > 0 && len(objectMeta.GetName()) == 0 {
   458→			return true
   459→		}

   462→}

   464→// createWithGenerateNameRetry attempts to create obj up to maxNameGenerationCreateAttempts
   465→// when create fails due to a name conflict error. Each attempt randomly generates a new
   466→// name based on generateName.
   467→func (e *Store) createWithGenerateNameRetry(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object, createValidation rest.ValidateObjectFunc, options *metav1.CreateOptions) (resultObj runtime.Object, err error) {
   468→	for i := 0; i < maxNameGenerationCreateAttempts; i++ {
   469→		resultObj, err = e.create(ctx, obj.DeepCopyObject(), createValidation, options)
   470→		if err == nil || !apierrors.IsAlreadyExists(err) {
   471→			return resultObj, err
   472→		}
   473→	}
   474→	return resultObj, err
   475→}

468\u2192\treturn c.storagemigrationV1alpha1\n   469\u2192}\n   470\u2192\n   471\u2192// Discovery retrieves the DiscoveryClient\n   472\u2192func (c *Clientset) Discovery() discovery.DiscoveryInterface {\n   473\u2192\tif c == nil {\n   474\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   475\u2192\t}\n   476\u2192\treturn c.DiscoveryClient\n   477\u2192}\n   478\u2192\n   479\u2192// NewForConfig creates a new Clientset for the given config.\n   480\u2192// If config's RateLimiter is not set and QPS and Burst are acceptable,\n   481\u2192// NewForConfig will generate a rate-limiter in configShallowCopy.\n   482\u2192// NewForConfig is equivalent to NewForConfigAndClient(c, httpClient),\n   483\u2192// where httpClient was generated with rest.HTTPClientFor(c).\n   484\u2192func NewForConfig(c *rest.Config) (*Clientset, error) {\n   485\u2192\tconfigShallowCopy := *c\n   486\u2192\n   487\u2192\tif configShallowCopy.UserAgent == \"\" {\n   488\u2192\t\tconfigShallowCopy.UserAgent = rest.DefaultKubernetesUserAgent()\n   489\u2192\t}\n   490\u2192\n   491\u2192\t// share the transport between all clients\n   492\u2192\thttpClient, err := rest.HTTPClientFor(&configShallowCopy)\n   493\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   494\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   495\u2192\t}\n   496\u2192\n   497\u2192\treturn NewForConfigAndClient(&configShallowCopy, httpClient)\n   498\u2192}\n   499\u2192\n   500\u2192// NewForConfigAndClient creates a new Clientset for the given config and http client.\n   501\u2192// Note the http client provided takes precedence over the configured transport values.\n   502\u2192// If config's RateLimiter is not set and QPS and Burst are acceptable,\n   503\u2192// NewForConfigAndClient will generate a rate-limiter in configShallowCopy.\n   504\u2192func NewForConfigAndClient(c *rest.Config, httpClient *http.Client) (*Clientset, error) {\n   505\u2192\tconfigShallowCopy := *c\n   506\u2192\tif configShallowCopy.RateLimiter == nil && configShallowCopy.QPS > 0 {\n   507\u2192\t\tif configShallowCopy.Burst <= 0 {\n   508\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"burst is required to be greater than 0 when RateLimiter is not set and QPS is set to greater than 0\")\n   509\u2192\t\t}\n   510\u2192\t\tconfigShallowCopy.RateLimiter = flowcontrol.NewTokenBucketRateLimiter(configShallowCopy.QPS, configShallowCopy.Burst)\n   511\u2192\t}\n   512\u2192\n   513\u2192\tvar cs Clientset\n   514\u2192\tvar err error\n   515\u2192\tcs.admissionregistrationV1, err = admissionregistrationv1.NewForConfigAndClient(&configShallowCopy, httpClient)\n   516\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   517\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   518\u2192\t}\n In `sg-benchmarks/kubernetes-client-go`, the typed Deployment client is implemented in `gentype/type.go`. The `Client[T].Create()` method (line 244) constructs and sends the HTTP request:\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (c *Client[T]) Create(ctx context.Context, obj T, opts metav1.CreateOptions) (T, error) {\\n    result := c.newObject()\\n    err := c.client.Post().\\n        UseProtobufAsDefaultIfPreferred(c.prefersProtobuf).\\n        NamespaceIfScoped(c.namespace, c.namespace != \\\"\\\").\\n        Resource(c.resource).\\n        VersionedParams(&opts, c.parameterCodec).\\n        Body(obj).\\n        Do(ctx).\\n        Into(result)\\n    return result, err\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThis method:\\n1. Creates a REST POST request builder via `c.client.Post()`\\n2. Configures the request with the resource name (\\\"deployments\\\"), namespace scope, and serialization preferences\\n3. Serializes the Deployment object as the request body\\n4. Executes the HTTP request via `Do(ctx)`, sending a POST to `/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments`\\n5. Deserializes the response into a result object\\n\\nThe actual HTTP transmission happens through the REST client's underlying transport layer, which sends the request to the Kubernetes API server endpoint.\\n\\n### Layer 2: Kubernetes API Server\\n\\nThe API server receives the POST request and routes it through its REST handler system. In `kubernetes/kubernetes`, Deployments are handled by the `REST` type defined in `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go` (line 88-90):\\n\\n```go\\ntype REST struct {\\n    *genericregistry.Store\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe `REST` handler is created by `NewREST()` (line 93), which initializes a `genericregistry.Store` with Deployment-specific strategies:\\n\\n```go\\nstore := &genericregistry.Store{\\n    NewFunc: func() runtime.Object { return &apps.Deployment{} },\\n    NewListFunc: func() runtime.Object { return &apps.DeploymentList{} },\\n    DefaultQualifiedResource: apps.Resource(\\\"deployments\\\"),\\n    CreateStrategy: deployment.Strategy,\\n    UpdateStrategy: deployment.Strategy,\\n    DeleteStrategy: deployment.Strategy,\\n    // ...\\n}\\n```\\n\\nWhen the REST handler processes the create request, it delegates to the `Store.Create()` method from `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` (line 446). This generic method:\\n\\n1. Calls `rest.BeforeCreate()` to invoke PrepareForCreate strategy hooks (e.g., clearing system-generated fields, setting Generation=1)\\n2. Invokes admission control plugins to allow or reject the Deployment\\n3. Calls validation via `createValidation` callback (which uses `appsvalidation.ValidateDeployment()`)\\n4. Persists the object via `e.Storage.Create()` to the etcd backend\\n5. Returns HTTP 201 Created to the client\\n\\nThe `CreateStrategy` (deployed.Strategy) implements validation rules specific to Deployments, such as validating replica counts, selector label matching, and pod template specifications.\\n\\n### Layer 3: Storage Backend (etcd)\\n\\nThe `Store.Create()` method calls `e.Storage.Create()`, which routes to the etcd3 storage backend in `kubernetes/kubernetes` at `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`. The etcd3 `store.Create()` method (line 241) translates the generic storage interface:\\n\\n1. Encodes the Deployment object using the appropriate codec (protobuf or JSON)\\n2. Calls `s.client.Kubernetes.OptimisticPut()` to initiate the etcd write\\n3. Handles conflict resolution and revision tracking for MVCC (Multi-Version Concurrency Control)\\n\\nThis delegates to the etcd distributed key-value store. In `etcd-io/etcd`, the `storeTxnWrite.Put()` method at `server/mvcc/kvstore_txn.go` (line 109) is the entry point:\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (tw *storeTxnWrite) Put(key, value []byte, lease lease.LeaseID) int64 {\\n    tw.put(key, value, lease)\\n    return tw.beginRev + 1\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe internal `put()` method (line 190) performs the critical steps:\\n\\n1. Generates a unique revision number for this write\\n2. Checks if the key previously existed (for update vs. insert semantics)\\n3. Marshals the Deployment into an `mvccpb.KeyValue` protobuf:\\n   ```go\\n   kv := mvccpb.KeyValue{\\n       Key: key,\\n       Value: value,\\n       CreateRevision: c,\\n       ModRevision: rev,\\n       Version: ver,\\n       Lease: int64(leaseID),\\n   }\\n   d, err := kv.Marshal()\\n   ```\\n4. Calls `tw.tx.UnsafeSeqPut(buckets.Key, ibytes, d)` at line 226 to write the marshaled data\\n5. Updates the in-memory index with `tw.s.kvindex.Put()` for fast future lookups\\n6. Records the change in `tw.changes` for transaction tracking\\n\\nFinally, the backend transaction's `UnsafeSeqPut()` method in `server/mvcc/backend/batch_tx.go` (line 145) executes the write to the underlying BoltDB store via `bucket.Put(key, value)`. This persists the Deployment to disk across the etcd cluster.\\n\\n### Complete Request Path\\n\\n```\\nClient Application\\n    \u2193\\nkubernetes-client-go: gentype/type.go:244 - Client.Create()\\n    \u2193 (HTTP POST)\\nKubernetes API Server\\n    \u2193\\nkubernetes/kubernetes: pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go:88 - REST handler\\n    \u2193\\nkubernetes/kubernetes: staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:446 - Store.Create()\\n    \u2193\\nkubernetes/kubernetes: staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go:241 - store.Create()\\n    \u2193\\netcd-io/etcd: server/mvcc/kvstore_txn.go:109 - storeTxnWrite.Put()\\n    \u2193\\netcd-io/etcd: server/mvcc/backend/batch_tx.go:145 - batchTx.UnsafeSeqPut()\\n    \u2193\\nBoltDB (Disk Persistence)\\n    \u2193\\nHTTP Response 201 Created\\n    \u2193\\nClient Application receives Deployment object\\n```\\n\\n### Key Design Insights\\n\\n1. **Separation of Concerns**: The client library knows nothing about REST endpoints\u2014it uses a generic REST client interface. The API server knows nothing about etcd internals\u2014it uses an abstract storage interface. This enables swapping implementations.\\n\\n2. **Strategy Pattern**: The `CreateStrategy` allows per-resource-type customization of validation and preparation without modifying core API server code.\\n\\n3. **MVCC Semantics**: etcd tracks multiple versions of each key, enabling watch-based updates and atomic compare-and-swap operations that Kubernetes relies on for coordination.\\n\\n4. **Revision Tracking**: Every Deployment creation increments etcd's revision counter, enabling clients to detect changes and synchronize cluster state.\\n\\n5. **Index Maintenance**: etcd's in-memory kvindex allows efficient key lookups without scanning the entire backend store on every read.\\n\\nThis architecture demonstrates Kubernetes' commitment to clean layering\u2014each component has a well-defined responsibility, and changes flow predictably through the system from client to durable storage.\"\n}\n",
